In contrast, the d-orbital electron cloud distribution in NaMoVS<sub>2</sub> is more numerous and larger, predicting a more favorable d-p orbital bonding. Calculations of projected density of states on dz2 and dxz/yz orbitals for NaVS<sub>2</sub> and NaMoVS<sub>2</sub> show that NaMoVS<sub>2</sub> has lower σ and π in the d orbital (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308630-fig-0006">6d</a>). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308630-fig-0006">6e,f</a> further show the d-p orbital hybridization state density and the corresponding energy intensity formed between NaVS<sub>2</sub>, NaMoVS<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>2</sub>S. It can be seen that the energy of the d-p orbital bonding electronic state between NaMoVS<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>2</sub>S decreases, which indicates that the d-p orbital bonding state increases. These results showed that after doping Mo, the intermediate product (Na<sub>x</sub>MoVS<sub>2</sub>) of the transformation reaction is able to form a more efficient d-p orbital hybridization with Na<sub>2</sub>S, and thus the intermediate product has a lower reaction barrier and decomposition potential, resulting in a better conversion reaction kinetics.</p>
         
         <p>Based on the excellent long cycle life and rate performance of Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub> anode, SIHC (denoted as 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC) was assembled with 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub> as the anode and commercial activated carbon (AC) as the cathode. The electrochemical performance of AC in the half-cell was tested first and the results are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> (Supporting Information). The CV curves are approximately rectangular, showing the typical characteristics of an electric double-layer capacitor (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11a</a>, Supporting Information). When the voltage reaches 4.2&nbsp;V, the CV curve of AC shows a strong oxidation peak, which is due to the oxidative decomposition of the electrolyte. So the voltage window is chosen to be 2–4&nbsp;V. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11b</a> (Supporting Information), the CV curve remains quasi-rectangular in shape with increasing scanning rates without serious distortion, which indicates its excellent reversibility. In addition, AC exhibits excellent rate performance (34 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>.) and long cycle stability (with 96.9% capacity retention after 3000 cycles at 1A g<sup>−1</sup>) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11c,d</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p><b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202308630-fig-0007">7a</a> shows a schematic diagram of the assembled SIHC device. During the charging of the SIHC, the anion (PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>) ions in the electrolyte are physically adsorbed onto the surface of the AC electrode, forming a double layer capacitance; At the same time, Na<sup>+</sup> ions inserted in the layers of Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub> and further happened phase conversion. The voltage window of SIHC and the N/P ratios of active materials are investigated with the results shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a> (Supporting Information). The CV curves and cycle performance reveal a voltage window of 1–4&nbsp;V. The mass ratio of cathode and anode of 1 : 2 demonstrated the best cycle stability, with an energy density of 78&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> and 90% retention after 3000 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202308630-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/96ccfa47-f119-46c7-a8c6-513a40688baf/smll202308630-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/96ccfa47-f119-46c7-a8c6-513a40688baf/smll202308630-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/bd1f9ada-b02b-4ae9-9869-6c4b4fe502e7/smll202308630-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/96ccfa47-f119-46c7-a8c6-513a40688baf/smll202308630-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202308630-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202308630" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic illustration of the 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC SIHC device. b) Charge/discharge curves at different current densities of the 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC SIHC. c) CV curves of 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC SIHC at various scan rates. d) Self-discharge curves of 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC SIHC after charging to 4&nbsp;V. e) Ragone diagram compared with other reported sulfide-based anode SIHCs, Na-ion batteries, and supercapacitors. f) Long-term cycle performance of the 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC SIHC at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Inset: photos of LEDs powered by 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC SIHC device.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308630-fig-0007">7b</a> shows the CV curves of the optimized 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC SIHC at different scan rates. It is clear that there is a slight deviation from the ideal rectangular shape of the CV curve of the SIHC due to the combination of different types of electrochemical mechanisms in the two electrodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308630-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0042_R_d23124618e2256" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - J. Power Sources">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Similarly, the quasi-triangular shape of the GCD curve (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308630-fig-0007">7c</a>) is caused by the combination of Faraday and non-Faraday processes present in the anode and cathode of the SIHC device.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308630-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0036_R_d23124618e2265" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Adv. Mater. Small Small Energy Environ. Mater. Adv. Sci.">36</a>, <a href="#smll202308630-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0043_R_d23124618e2265" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Nano-Micro Lett. J. Power Sources Adv. Sci.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the profiles of the CV and GCD curves remain essentially constant with increasing scan rate and current density without significant distortion, indicating excellent reversibility and excellent rate capability. Self-discharge performance is also a key parameter to evaluate the commercial prospect of energy storage devices. The presence of self-discharge not only leads to a reduction in the capacity of the device itself, but also seriously affects the battery assembly and cycle life. Its self-discharge curve (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308630-fig-0007">7d</a>) with an open-circuit voltage that remains at ≈3.62&nbsp;V after 450 h, exhibiting low self-discharge rate compared to the similar devices reported.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308630-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0008_R_d23124618e2273" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater. Energy Storage Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#smll202308630-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0043_R_d23124618e2273" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Nano-Micro Lett. J. Power Sources Adv. Sci.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308630-fig-0007">7e</a> shows the Ragone diagram of this work with other reported sulfide-based anode SIHCs,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308630-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0044_R_d23124618e2282" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - ACS Nano">44</a>-<a href="#smll202308630-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0049_R_d23124618e2282" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Energy Storage Mater.">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Na-ion batteries,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308630-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0050_R_d23124618e2287" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Adv. Sci.">50</a>-<a href="#smll202308630-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0052_R_d23124618e2287" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Nano-Micro Lett.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and supercapacitors.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308630-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0053_R_d23124618e2292" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - J. Energy Storage">53</a>-<a href="#smll202308630-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308630-bib-0055_R_d23124618e2292" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It can be seen that the hybrid device has the advantages of high energy density and high power density. The 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC SIHC exhibits an energy density of 98&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 218&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>, while it maintains a satisfactory energy density of 59&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 11&nbsp;840&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>, better than many previously reported SIHCs. The 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC SIHCs exhibit excellent cycling stability, with capacity retention of 85% for 15&nbsp;000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup> with coulombic efficiencies of almost 100% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308630-fig-0007">7f</a>). The excellent electrochemical performance is superior to that previously reported in the SIHC (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). In addition, the 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>//AC device can illuminate the “SIHC” symbol consisting of light emitting diodes (LEDs) in parallel, further demonstrating its potential for practical applications.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202308630-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202308630-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>The nanostructure and electronic properties of VS<sub>2</sub> are engineered by means of NH<sub>4</sub><sup>+</sup> pre-intercalation and Mo doping. Experimental results reveal the NH<sub>4</sub><sup>+</sup> pre-intercalation enlarges the interplanar spacing of VS<sub>2</sub> and the volume expansion during cycling is mitigated. Meanwhile, Mo doping in VS<sub>2</sub> further provides additional Na<sup>+</sup> storage sites according to formation of double defects at interlayer and sulfur vacancies. Those structure engineering unblock new cross-layer migration pathways to realize Na<sup>+</sup> transportion along three-dimensional direction. Mo doping is found to further enhance the d-p orbital hybridization between Na<sub>x</sub>VS<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>2</sub>S and improve the electrochemical conversion power of Na<sub>x</sub>VS<sub>2</sub>. Thus, 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub> demonstrated excellent rate performance (453 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 3 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and long cycling life (over 20&nbsp;000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>). The assembled SIHCs achieve impressive maximum energy density/power density of 98&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>/11.84&nbsp;kW kg<sup>−1</sup>, ultralong cycling life over 15&nbsp;000 cycles (capacity retention: 85%) and very low self-discharge rate (0.84&nbsp;mV h<sup>−1</sup>). This work provides a simple and innovative modification strategy to effectively enhance the electrochemical kinetics of conversion-type metal sulfide anode, deciphering the modulation essence of the d-p hybridization state during the transformation reaction, offering valuable insight for developing high-performance anode materials for SIHCs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202308630-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202308630-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308630-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308630-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308630-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202308630-sec-0070-title"> Synthesis of Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub></h4>
                  
                  <p>Mo-doping and NH<sub>4</sub><sup>+</sup> pre-intercalation VS<sub>2</sub> were carried out by one-step solvothermal method. Typically, (2-x) mmol vanadyl acetylacetonate (VO(acac)<sub>2</sub>), x mmol molybdenyl acetylacetonate (Mo(acac)<sub>2</sub>), (<i>x</i> = 0.03, 0.05, 0.10, 0.20) and 10&nbsp;mmol thioacetamide (TAA) were dissolved in 40&nbsp;mL dimethylacetamide (DMA), followed by vigorously stirred at room temperature for 1&nbsp;h. The obtained homogeneous solution was then transferred into a 100&nbsp;mL Teflon-lined stainless-steel autoclave for solvothermal reaction at 200°C for 16&nbsp;h. After natural cooling to room temperature, the black precipitates were washed with deionized water and ethanol for several times and then freeze-dried for 24&nbsp;h. The NH<sub>4</sub><sup>+</sup> pre-intercalation VS<sub>2</sub> with different Mo-doping concentrations was named as 3%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>, 5%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>, 10%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>, 20%Mo-NVS<sub>2</sub>. For comparative study, VS<sub>2</sub> with NH<sub>4</sub><sup>+</sup> pre-intercalation was synthesized by the same process without Mo(acac)<sub>2</sub>, which is named as NVS<sub>2</sub>. The VS<sub>2</sub> with normal layer spacing can be obtained by annealing the NVS<sub>2</sub> at 400°C under argon atmosphere for 2&nbsp;h, which is named annealed VS<sub>2</sub>.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308630-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202308630-sec-0080-title"> Material Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The morphology and crystal structure of all samples were observed by field-emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM, Hitachi SU8010) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM, FEI TALOS F200X). The powder X-ray diffraction (XRD) pattern was collected by X Pert PRO MPD diffractometer under Cu Kα radiation. Raman spectra were obtained by ThermoScientific Dxr2 xi spectrometer with 532&nbsp;nm excitation wavelength. The elemental composition and chemical state of the sample surface were analyzed by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, Thermo Scientific K-Alpha, Al Ka radiation). The BET test was performed using a specific surface and porosity analyzer (Micromeritics ASAP 2460) to evaluate the surface area and pore size distribution. Thermal decomposition process of samples were measured by differential scanning calorimeter (DSC, TA Q20) at a rate of 5 °C min<sup>−1</sup> from room temperature to 300 °C in N<sub>2</sub> atmosphere. The content of Mo element was measured by ICP-OES (Agilent 5110). The sulfur vacancies in the samples were analyzed by electron paramagnetic resonance (EPR, Bruker EMXnano).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308630-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202308630-sec-0090-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The working electrode prepared by mixing 70&nbsp;wt.% active material, 20&nbsp;wt.% acetylene black, and 10&nbsp;wt.% polyvinylidene difluoride (PVDF) binder in N-methyl-2-pyrrolidone (NMP) solvent. The resulting slurry was then evenly coated on copper foil and dried at 65°C in a vacuum drying oven for 12&nbsp;h. The mass loading of the active material was 1.2–1.5&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. The sodium metal sheet with a diameter of 15.6&nbsp;mm was used as the counter electrode, the glass fiber GF/D was used as the separator, and 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> in DME was used as the electrolyte. Then CR2032 type coin cell was assembled in a glove box filled with argon and H<sub>2</sub>O, O<sub>2</sub> contents both less than 1&nbsp;ppm. Galvanostatic charge and discharge measurements were performed on a Neware battery test system (BTS-5V-20&nbsp;mA) at 30°C within a voltage window of 0.3–3.0&nbsp;V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na. The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) tests were performed over the same voltage range. 150 cycles were performed on each electrode to reach steady state before the GITT test. The test had a constant current time of 10 min, a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and a relaxation time of 30 min. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) was tested by electrochemical workstation (CHI760E). Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) tests were performed in the frequency range of 10<sup>−2</sup>–10<sup>5</sup>&nbsp;Hz.</p>
                  
                  <p>The SIHC was assembled using pre-sodiated 5%Mo-VS<sub>2</sub> as anode and activated carbon (Kararuy, YP-50) as cathode. The weight ratios of anode and cathode were 1:1, 1:2, 1:3, 1:4, and 1:5, respectively. Before being assembled into SIHCs, the anode was assembled into a half cell and discharged to 0.3&nbsp;V after three cycles at a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. The cathode was prepared by dissolving 70 wt.% AC, 20 wt.% acetylene black and 10 wt.% PVDF binder in NMP and then coating on aluminum foil. The energy density and power density of the SIHC device are based on the total mass of the anode and cathode.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308630-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202308630-sec-0100-title"> Computational Methods</h4>
                  
                  <p><i>Density of States and Diffusion Energy Barriers Calculations</i>: First-principles calculation was performed by using quantum espresso package on the basis of density functional theory (DFT). Ultrasoft pseudopotential (USP) was used to treat the core electrons. The electron exchange-correlation energy was approximated by the generalized gradient approximation-Perdew-Burke-Ernzerhof (GGA-PBE) functional. For the self-consistent calculation, a real-space resolution was set to be 0.3 Bohr. The tolerances of total energy and charge density were converged to 1×10<sup>–6</sup> Ry and 1×10<sup>–6</sup>, respectively. The Brillouin zone electron structure integrations were performed by using 6×7×6 Monkhorst-Pack scheme K-point mesh sampling. Diffusion energy barriers was calculated by collecting single point energies of the each stage of the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion models.</p>
                  
                  <p><i>Orbital Hybridization Calculation</i>: Gaussian package was used for orbital calculation with Hartree–Fock (HF) method. The lanl2mb basis set was used for geometry optimization and single point energy calculation, with an energy convergency threshold 1×10<sup>−7</sup> Ry.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
